{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 15:33:24","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 15:33:24","title":"All the upcoming Chrome OS devices and boards we’re tracking right now [UPDATE: 9/4/2020]","link":"https://chromeunboxed.com/?p=18348","description":"<a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" title=\"All the upcoming Chrome OS devices and boards we&#8217;re tracking right now [UPDATE: 9/4/2020]\" rel=\"nofollow\"><img width=\"1024\" height=\"711\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020-1024x711.jpg\" class=\"webfeedsFeaturedVisual wp-post-image\" alt=\"\" loading=\"lazy\" style=\"display: block; margin: auto; margin-bottom: 10px;max-width: 100%;\" link_thumbnail=\"1\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020-1024x711.jpg 1024w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020-300x208.jpg 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020-768x533.jpg 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020-1536x1066.jpg 1536w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020.jpg 2000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" data-attachment-id=\"13413\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-chrome-os-tablets-early-2020/newwavechromebooksearly2020/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"2000,1388\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020-300x208.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/NewWaveChromebooksEarly2020-1024x711.jpg\" /></a>\n<p id=\"update\"><strong>UPDATE &#8211; 9/4/2020: </strong>Based on the recent finds, we&#8217;re adding quite a few devices to the mix today.  We have some Tiger Lake Chromebooks, some AMD Chromebooks, some new MediaTek 8183 Chromebooks, and some Jasper Lake Chromebooks to add to the ever-expanding list in this update, so take a look!</p>\n\n\n\n<p>From time to time, it is useful to get your thoughts in one place.  As we continue to track new baseboards and upcoming Chrome OS devices on a daily basis, it can become a bit confusing for us as writers and for you as readers exactly which board is expected to do what.  A few years ago, we&#8217;d be tracking a handful of devices, see those devices arrive, and move on to looking for more.  It was pretty easy to keep all the newness in front of us back then, <strong>but it&#8217;s a very different story these days.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Looking at my notes and my starred/saved changes from the Chromium Repositories, there are <strong><em>so many</em></strong> new devices in development across multiple different baseboards with a wide assortment of chip sets, configurations, and form factors.  As I began looking across all those boards and upcoming devices, it hit me that we&#8217;d do well to take some inventory of where we are, where we&#8217;re going, and what all these code-names and baseboards have to do with upcoming Chromebooks.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>A quick note in the event that all this is new to you:</strong> baseboards and overlays are code-named in the open source Chromium Repositories and usually exist these days in a particular structure.  There are unibuild boards that spawn multiple different devices with their own code-named overlays.  These devices will be similar on the inside, but each one could be a different Chromebook made by a different manufacturer.  The recently released Lenovo Flex 5 and ASUS Chromebook C436 are both based on the unibuild &#8216;Hatch&#8217; baseboard, for example, and are quite different on the outside. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>There&#8217;s a lot of info to take in here, so this is how we&#8217;ll proceed:</strong> we&#8217;ll put each main, unibuild board as a heading, explain what the main features are of that board, and then list the overlays and devices being built off of that board.  We&#8217;ll link the lists to what we know about these upcoming Chromebooks so you can research further if you&#8217;d like. So, with that in mind, let&#8217;s dive in and see everything we know about at this point in 2020.</p>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Kukui&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>The &#8216;Kukui&#8217; baseboard is the unibuild that has already spawned the Lenovo 10e and the Chromebook Duet.  We know there are more devices coming based on this board with the possibility of at least one more tablet/detachable variant.  These Chromebooks will run on the MediaTek P60T chip set and, like the Duet, will be decent performers with great battery life.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/unboxing-the-lenovo-chromebook-duet/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Krane&#8217; (Lenovo Chromebook Duet)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/lenovo-chromebook-10e-duet-tablet-preview/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kodama&#8217; (Lenovo Chromebook 10e)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebook-in-the-works-where-are-you-qualcomm/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Jacuzzi&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebooks-four-new-devices-in-the-works/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Damu&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebooks-four-new-devices-in-the-works/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kappa&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebooks-four-new-devices-in-the-works/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kakadu&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-chromebooks-four-new-devices-in-the-works/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Juniper&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Willow&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Burnet&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Esche&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Hatch&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>The &#8216;Hatch&#8217; baseboard is based on the 10th-gen Intel Comet Lake chips and these Chromebooks come with an armada of upgrades over their 8th-gen predecessors.  &#8216;Hatch&#8217;-based Chromebooks will have faster performance, WiFi 6, Bluetooth 5, optional NVMe storage, fingerprint scanners, pen support, and premium build options.  However, &#8216;Hatch&#8217; boards can also spawn devices like the Lenovo Flex 5 Chromebook that bring much of the goodness of the latest-gen hardware and keep the price in check.  An additional feature of these Chromebooks is or will be the inclusion of regular updates until June of 2028.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/samsung-galaxy-chromebook-review/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kohaku&#8217; (Samsung Galaxy Chromebook)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/asus-chromebook-flip-c436-review/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Helios&#8217; (ASUS Chromebook Flip C436)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/lenovo-flex-5-chromebook-most-important-of-the-year/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Akemi&#8217; (Lenovo Flex 5 Chromebook)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-hatch-kindred-helios-kohaku-intel-powerful-fast-comet-lake/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kindred&#8217;</a> <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/acer-chromebook-712-durable-rugged-education-schools-hands-on/\" target=\"_blank\">(Acer Chromebook 712)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebook-kled-hatch-family-devices/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Kled&#8217; </a><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/acer-chromebook-spin-713-review-flagship-affordable/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">(Acer Chromebook Spin 713)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/hp-launches-3-new-10th-gen-intel-chromebook-for-enterprise/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Dratini&#8217; (HP Pro C640 Chromebook)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/hp-launches-3-new-10th-gen-intel-chromebook-for-enterprise/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Dragonair&#8217; (HP Elite C1030 Chromebook)</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/integrated-privacy-screens-are-headed-to-chromebooks-later-this-year/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Drallion&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/upcoming-chromebook-jinlon-getting-a-mysterious-feature-weve-not-seen-before/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Jinlon&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mushu-chromebook-discrete-gpu-project-athena/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Mushu&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/stryke-chromebook-10th-gen-comet-lake-intel-hatch-development/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Stryke&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/asus-chromebook-flip-c436-palkia-affordable/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Palkia&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/nightfury-new-samsung-galaxy-chromebook-plus/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Nightfury&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/comet-lake-chromeboxes-are-headed-our-way-hello-puff/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Puff&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Volteer&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>While we still have a long way to go in getting all the upcoming 10th-gen Comet Lake devices out of development and into users&#8217; hands, that doesn&#8217;t mean the Chrome OS developers are just sitting by on the current generation.  Instead, things are continuing to move forward on the latest, greatest chips from Intel in the form of the 11th-gen Tiger Lake 10nm processors.  These devices started development at the end of 2019, so don&#8217;t expect to see anything from this group until the end of 2020 or at shows like CES 2021 next year.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-begins-prepping-for-intels-10nm-tiger-lake-cpu/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Volteer&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/tiger-lake-chromebook-10nm-deltaur-development/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Deltaur&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/lenovo-chromebook-intel-tiger-lake-11th-gen-malefor/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Malefor&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-10nm-tiger-lake-chromebook-discovered-meet-ripto/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Ripto&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/three-new-tiger-lake-chromebooks-in-the-works-asus-is-in-the-mix/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Mudada&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/three-new-tiger-lake-chromebooks-in-the-works-asus-is-in-the-mix/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Terrador&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/three-new-tiger-lake-chromebooks-in-the-works-asus-is-in-the-mix/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Delbin&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Lingcod&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Lindar&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Todor&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Eldrid&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Asurada&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/mediatek-5g-soc-premium-chromebook-processor/\" target=\"_blank\">This board, for the time being, stands alone.</a>  Think of &#8216;Asurada&#8217; as a tangent to &#8216;Kukui&#8217; but also as an upgrade.  The chip on board for this one is the MediaTek 8192 and it is a substantial upgrade over the 8183 (also called the Helio P60T) that is found in &#8216;Kukui&#8217; devices.  With the underlying similarities to &#8216;Kukui&#8217;, we expect development to move fast with &#8216;Asurada&#8217; and we&#8217;d expect it to spawn quite a few boards in the coming months.</p>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Zork&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>While we&#8217;ve become accustomed to seeing the latest Intel chips in new Chromebook boards, it is really awesome to see higher-powered AMD chips being worked on for use in a handful of upcoming Chromebooks.  We had a small wave of affordable AMD devices last year, but those were based on the older A4 and A6 chips that offered little in the way of upgrades from the more-affordable mobile Intel processors.  With these new Picasso chips from AMD, Intel may finally have a fight on its hands for top-tier Chromebook performance.  Additionally, there are a couple boards below that are a sort of tandem to &#8216;Zork&#8217; in &#8216;Dalboz&#8217; and &#8216;Ezkinil&#8217; that are swapping the AMD Picasso chips for the newer, more-mobile focused Dali processors.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebook-zork-takes-amd-to/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Zork&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-mobile-processors-athlon-ryzen-dali-chromebooks/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Trembyle&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-ryzen-picasso-chromebook-morphius-vega-graphics/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Morphius&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebook-picasso-apu-ces-2020/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Mandolin&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-mobile-processors-athlon-ryzen-dali-chromebooks/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Dalboz&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-mobile-processors-athlon-ryzen-dali-chromebooks/\">&#8216;Ezkinil&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebooks-zork-two-new-boards-development/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Vilboz&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebooks-zork-two-new-boards-development/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Berknip&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Dirinboz&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Woomax&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Trogdor&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>This chip set is one we&#8217;ve been looking at for a very, very long time.  &#8216;Trogdor&#8217; is the torch-bearer for what we hope will become the first Qualcomm Snapdragon Chromebook.  In development for years already, we used to keep tabs on &#8216;Cheza&#8217; as the first possible Snapdragon device, but it looks like &#8216;Cheza&#8217; may never materialize as it is based on the Snapdragon 845 chip that is rapidly becoming obsolete.  Instead, &#8216;Trogdor&#8217; looks to leverage the newer Snapdragon Compute 7c chip set that makes far more sense in Chromebooks.  </p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/qualcomm-snapdragon-7c-chromebook/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Trogdor&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-tablet-phone-snapdragon-screen/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Bubs&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/qualcomm-snapdragon-7c-chromebook-development-lazor-trogdor/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Lazor&#8217;</a></li><li>&#8216;<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/?s=cheza\" target=\"_blank\">Cheza</a>&#8216;</li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/pompom-qualcomm-snapdragon-chromebook-production-compal-quanta-coming-soon/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Pompom&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/snapdragon-7c-chromebook-limozeen-trogdor\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25207\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Limozeen&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h4>&#8216;Dedede&#8217;</h4>\n\n\n\n<p>We only know a bit about this board, but the main highlight is the Jasper Lake Intel processors that will retain the low price of Intel&#8217;s small core, mobile-focused chips while giving users a very nice speed bump over the current Gemini Lake Chromebooks.  There aren&#8217;t many of these yet, but expect a ton to show up as 2020 rolls on.</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebook-dedede-begins-development-with-rumored-10nm-intel-jasper-lake-processor/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Dedede&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebook-dedede-begins-development-with-rumored-10nm-intel-jasper-lake-processor/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;WaddleDoo&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/3-new-chromebooks-development-boards-tiger-lake-jasper-lake-intel/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;WaddleDee&#8217;</a></li><li><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/3-new-chromebooks-development-boards-tiger-lake-jasper-lake-intel/\" target=\"_blank\">&#8216;Magolor&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Drawcia&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Boten&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-chromebooks-development-volteer-zork-kukui-dedede\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Madoo&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>As time goes by, we&#8217;ll regularly update this post with new boards we find and new news we come across on boards we already have good knowledge about.</strong>  We&#8217;re hopeful this becomes a place you can regularly return to that you may stay up to date on all the Chromebooks on the way.  We thought last year was crazy, but this is already at a whole new level in 2020.  Bookmark this post to stay in the know&#8230;<strong>it&#8217;s going to be a fun ride!</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener daily basis as we feel quite certain at this point that <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-pixelbook-2-assistant-key-proof-halvor-tiger-lake\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24972\" target=\"_blank\">this Chromebook is none other than the Pixelbook 2 in development.</a>  With some additional clues in the form of the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/halvor-pixelbook-2-chromebook-made-by-google\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25063\" target=\"_blank\">Pixelbook-specific keyboard top row layout,</a> things just keep adding up to make the case for &#8216;Halvor&#8217; as a new Pixelbook.  Today&#8217;s additions to the &#8216;Halvor&#8217; narrative aren&#8217;t clues that point toward Google, though.  Instead, as we&#8217;re still trying to nail down more proof on the idea that this is a Google-made Chromebook, we wanted to share details we find about this upcoming device as we find them.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>USB 4.0 is on the way for Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25254\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-pixelbook-2-halvor-usb-4-thunderbolt/halvor-usb-4-thunderbolt/\" sizes=\"(max-width: 607px) 100vw, 607px\" /><figcaption><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2311998/10/board/halvor/board.h#79\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Via the Chromium Gerrit</a></figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-prepares-to-embrace-usb-4-0/\">We&#8217;ve talked about USB 4.0</a> and the potential for it hitting a next-gen Chromebook already, but I&#8217;ll quickly recap why its a big deal.  For one, USB 4.0 will unify USB under one connector: USB Type C.  If it utilizing USB 4.0, it will have the Type C connector.  <strong>No more confusion there.</strong>  Additionally, we&#8217;re looking at 40GB/s transfer speeds, Thunderbolt 3, PD (power deliver for fast charging standards) and backwards compatibility with older USB 3.2 and USB 2.0 protocols.  This is a next-gen connectivity standard we will all come to expect as we move into 2021, so I&#8217;m glad to see &#8216;Halvor&#8217; will come equipped with it.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Thunderbolt is finally coming to Chromebooks, too</h2>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-thunderbolt-3-support-chrome-os/\" target=\"_blank\">We&#8217;ve talked about Thunderbolt support for Chromebooks</a> on multiple occasions and, honestly, we thought we&#8217;d eventually see it hit a &#8216;Hatch&#8217;-based Chromebook like the Samsung Galaxy Chromebook or Acer Spin 713, but there&#8217;s been no real movement on that front with the current generation of Chromebooks.  Tiger Lake Chromebooks based on the &#8216;Volteer&#8217; baseboard, on the other hand, look set to deliver the benefits of Thunderbolt to Chrome OS and &#8216;Halvor&#8217; definitely looks to be getting in on the action.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The benefits?  Thunderbolt greatly increases data transfer speeds for things like external GPUs and SSDs, but is also plays a very important role in giving Chromebooks a far greater ability to leverage multiple external displays at once.  While not a tool every user is after right now, the additional headroom is definitely welcome on higher-end Chromebooks from a productivity standpoint and, with the addition of both USB 4.0 and Thunderbolt, it appears Google&#8217;s next Chromebook won&#8217;t be at a loss for external data transfer prowess.</p>\n\n\n\n<img While we haven&#8217;t seen anything official about the update going live, Google has announced some new features for Chrome OS. Presumably, these features will be part of the update when it does happen. These updates may seem relatively insignificant in relation to the past few Chrome OS versions but they bring some very useful features to users that&#8217;s what we love to see. We&#8217;ll keep looking for an actual device to update and let you know when it looks like the rollout is live. In the meantime, here&#8217;s what&#8217;s new and headed our way in Chrome OS. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Wi-Fi Sync</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Syncing Wi-Fi passwords across devices may not be the first thing you think of when you&#8217;re logging into a new Chromebook. Most of us are used to uses a device for the first time and setting up the network before logging in. However, with Wi-Fi Sync, you&#8217;ll wish Google had done this years ago. The new feature will sync Wi-Fi credentials to your profile &#8220;keychain&#8221; and carry it to any other device you log into. It may seem like a minor thing but think about all the times you went to your parents&#8217; house and had to get the insanely long password off the back of the router that&#8217;s behind the television where dust bunnies go to die. Yeah, it&#8217;s a pain. Wi-Fi Sync is a brilliant addition to an ecosystem already designed to keep your data synced across devices. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25192\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/whats-new-with-chrome-os-85-wi-fi-sync-play-pause-video-and-more/screenshot_2020-08-31_at_5-09-09_pm-max-1000x1000-1/\" Google</figcaption></figure>\n\n\n\n<h2>Simpler, smarter search</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Currently, searching for an item in the Chrome OS settings menu is limited to exact search terms. For example, if I search &#8220;wi-fi&#8221; on Chrome OS 84, I will see any wi-fi-related settings highlighted in yellow. If I change the search term to &#8220;wifi,&#8221; I get nothing. Chrome OS 85 will bring a more intuitive settings search and even give you suggestions for items that may be related to the setting your are seeking. Building on this new feature, future updates will add this search feature to the app launcher. Google states that this is part of the company&#8217;s goal to make the Launcher an &#8220;everything button.&#8221; </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gallery columns-1 is-cropped\"><ul bring more granular controls to your microphone. Users will be able to open the audio settings in the system tray and manually adjust mic levels with a convenient slider. Perfect if your audience is having a little trouble hearing you. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Microphone_control_1.gif\" alt=\"\"/></figure>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/the-best-chromebooks-of-2020-so-far/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-19547\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/bestChromebooksOf2020soFar-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"The best Chromebooks of 2020 so far [VIDEO]\" title=\"The best Chromebooks of 2020 so far [VIDEO]\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">The best Chromebooks of 2020 so far [VIDEO]</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/robbypayne/\">Robby Payne</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<h2>Camera tools</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Chrome OS recently changed the default file type the camera to .mp4. This was a much-needed update as this file type is supported by the majority of devices we use on a daily basis. To make the camera even more capable, Chrome OS 85 will add the ability to pause and start video recording so you can create one continuous video file without taking any breaks. You&#8217;ll also be able to capture still images while recording video which is a feature that should be a part of any decent camera.  </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-uniblog-publish-prod/original_images/Untitled__Aug_20_2020_5_21_PM_3.gif\" alt=\"\"/></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>As I said, Chrome OS 85 is scheduled to arrive today. As of the publishing of this article, we haven&#8217;t seen any sign that the server has updated any devices to 85 but we&#8217;ll keep a close watch and update you when it begins to roll out. I&#8217;m anxious to see what other features may come along for the ride. Did you get the update to Chrome OS 85? data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/virtualDesksWorkflowChromebookFeature-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>I remember a point in time when I would <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/?s=virtual+desks\" target=\"_blank\">write about Virtual Desks on Chrome OS with painful regularity.</a>  I was insanely excited about this feature coming to Chromebooks and tracked every little change and detail until it was <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-80-virtual-desktops-4-finger-gesture-switch-stable-no-flags/\" target=\"_blank\">rolled-out in fullness in March of this year.</a>  Since that time, there&#8217;s not been a whole lot of development on this highly-useful feature apart from <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-83-brings-persistent-virtual-desks/\" target=\"_blank\">the ability to rename your desks</a> and, honestly, I&#8217;m OK with that.  The feature has been so solid and great to use that it has become a regular part of my daily workflow and one I have a hard time imagining living without.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>It looks like a solid upgrade will be coming to Virtual Desks via a small-but-helpful change for people that like to use these desks as a legitimate productivity tool.  <a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2376418\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">According to this commit from the Chromium Repositories,</a> Virtual Desks are getting an upgrade in the speed department that will allow quick moves between all four desks to happen with much higher rates of speed.  </p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>desks: Allow multiple keyboard press to switch desks quickly. </p><p>Second CL to allow chaining keyboard shortcuts. </p><p>Follow up to <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"http://crrev.com/c/2354798\" target=\"_blank\">crrev.com/c/2354798</a> which allows RootWindowDeskSwitch to handle more than two screenshots. This CL fills it out by handling taking third and fourth screenshots and placing them on the animation layer to get a nice smooth continuous animation. Tests in a follow up.</p><cite><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2376418\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p>As it stands right now, if you use the keyboard shortcut to move through your open desks <strong>( SEARCH + [ or ] )</strong>, you&#8217;ll notice you can only move to the next desk once the desk you just jumped to slides fully into view.  Hit that shortcut key before the animation finishes and nothing happens.  What this means is jumping from desk 1 to desk 4 can take a few seconds at best and a tad longer at worst.  </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If, like me, you use Virtual Desks on a regular basis, this can add up to a lot of wasted time moving through your open desks.  I tend to put the same stuff on my desks every day, so I always know that my music player and related media is always on my 4th desk, for instance, and moving to that desk from my 1st desk (where my primary stuff lives) takes a second or two no matter how I go about doing it.  Not a huge headache, but I can easily see where quicker transitions could go a long way.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This upcoming change should allow users to move from desk to desk with much less time between animations, meaning if you are on desk 1 and need to skip right to desk 4, you can hit that keyboard shortcut 3 times in succession and land right on the desk you need without waiting for animations to load each time.  For users that are invested in using Virtual Desks on their Chromebook, this tiny change could go a long way towards saving us all quite a bit of time.  We&#8217;ll be on the lookout for this change to be merged and will give it a try in the Canary Channel as soon as we see it arrive.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ctl-nl81-14-chromebook-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>Chromebooks are scarce. If you&#8217;ve looked around the web in an attempt to find a decent device at a price that doesn&#8217;t induce a stroke, you probably know exactly what I&#8217;m talking about. As of this morning, Best Buy had less than six Chromebook models in stock and three of those were variants of the Pixelbook Go. While most manufacturers are working diligently to get new models into the market, it looks like late fall is going to be the earliest we see most devices back in stock on a regular basis. CTL has been at the mercy of high demand and short supply like everyone else but that hasn&#8217;t stopped the Oregon-base Chromebook maker from getting some new products in the pipeline.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In a company first, CTL has debuted two 14&#8243; Chromebooks and these devices are looking to shake up the mid-range Chrome OS market thanks to some impressive specs with a very palatable price tag. For starters, CTL&#8217;s base model 14&#8243; Chromebook comes out of the gate with a Full HD display which is not the norm when we&#8217;re talking EDU devices. Both devices feature Intel Gemini Lake-R CPUs that boasts processing power that&#8217;s more than ample for the majority of users. I&#8217;m not just talking about your middle school student, either. We&#8217;ll talk a little more about that in a second. For now, let&#8217;s take a look at the new Chromebooks from CTL. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>CTL Chromebook NL81</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The entry-level 14&#8243; Chromebook NL81 features a Full HD anti-glare panel which should make for a great workspace. It is powered by the dual-core Intel Gemini Lake-R N4020 which we have seen in a handful of devices as of late. As you can see in <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/lenovo-chromebook-ideapad-3-review-cheap-good-review/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19638\" target=\"_blank\">our review of the Lenovo Chromebook 3</a>, this small core CPU is a workhorse and will chew threw anything the average user can throw at it. This model is paired with 4GB of RAM and 32GB of storage. It&#8217;s a bit scant on that end but let&#8217;s remember, this is and EDU device. 4GB is still enough when used in conjunction with a decent processor. For the storage, you do get a MicroSD card slot and of course, you have Google Drive right there in your files app. Moving on. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>As with all CTL Chromebooks, this model features its own share of rugged specifications. The keyboard is spill-resistant and the keys are anti-peel. We&#8217;ll have to get our hands on the NL81 to see just how tough it is but CTL does state that it is drop-tested with an IP rating and a non-slip design. Oh yeah, it also has Bluetooth 5 and Gigabit Wi-Fi. It&#8217;s not quite a zippy as Wi-Fi 6 but I doubt you&#8217;ll notice. Here&#8217;s a closer look at the CTL Chromebook NL81: </p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Chrome OS</strong></li><li><strong>Processor</strong>: Intel Gemini Lake R N4020</li><li><strong>RAM:</strong>&#160;4GB LPDDR4</li><li><strong>Storage:</strong>&#160;32GB eMMC</li><li><strong>Camera:</strong>&#160;HD 720P with LED indicator</li><li><strong>GPU:</strong>&#160;Intel® UMA GLK-R&#160;Integrated Graphics</li><li><strong>Display:</strong>&#160;16:9 14&#8243; 1920 X 1080p FHD LED Anti-Glare</li><li><strong>Ports:&#160;</strong>2x USB 3.0, 2x USB-C with PD function, 2-in-1 SD/MMC Card Reader, Audio Combo Jack</li><li><strong>Audio:&#160;</strong>Single Digital Microphone</li><li><strong>WLAN</strong>:&#160;WL/BT 802.11ABGN/AC 9560.NGWG.NV, Intel® 9560 Wireless, MU-MIMO support</li><li><strong>AUE June 2026</strong></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>Here&#8217;s the best part of this device. It is available for pre-order for the discounted price of $279. The MSRP will eventually be $349 but I&#8217;d argue that you&#8217;d be hard-pressed to find another device, available or not, that carries this kind of price tag and offers this much in the way of specs. For reference, Acer&#8217;s Chromebook 314 has a 1366&#215;768 panel, the older N4000 CPU, and retails for $249. You may not think it would make a big difference but believe me, your eyes will appreciate having a FullHD panel and the performance boost of the N4020 is worth the extra few bucks, in my opinion. The Chromebook NL81 won&#8217;t ship until Nov/Dec but pre-orders are up and you will snag that discount if you reserve now. I know that doesn&#8217;t help if you need a Chromebook right now but this will be a great option for schools looking to boost their laptop fleets as we round out 2020. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><a This processor puts up Octane scores over 21,000 in devices that we have tested and this Chromebook gets the added boost of 8GB of RAM and 64GB of storage. It features the same rugged specs and generous port selection. Acer&#8217;s comparable model will retail for $429 but CTL is listing the NL81T for only $379 and you&#8217;re getting the exact same performance on top of the durability that CTL is known for in its Chromebooks. Pre-orders are open and the Chromebook NL81T will ship in late November or early December. We&#8217;ll get these in the office ASAP and let you know if the CTL NL81 will be the Chromebook to beat in this segment. </p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Chrome With so many of us working or learning from home, it is imperative that we can access coverage in every corner of our home or office. Google&#8217;s Nest Wi-Fi is one of the best solutions around to do just that. The Nest Wi-Fi router is capable of delivering upwards of 600 Mbps to a single device and it will cover up to 2200 sq. ft. When you toss in an add-on Nest Point, you can cover as much as 3800 sq. ft. and you&#8217;ll get the added bonus of a Google Assistant-enabled smart speaker. </p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/googles-nest-wifi-is-now-available-read-this-before-you-buy/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-12559\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/nestwifipoint-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"Google&#039;s Nest Wifi is now available: Read this before you buy\" title=\"Google&#039;s Nest Wifi is now available: Read this before you buy\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">Google&#8217;s Nest Wifi is now available: Read this before you buy</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/gabe/\">Gabriel Brangers</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<p>If you&#8217;re looking to get a larger space setup for better internet access, Woot! has a deal for you. The two add-on points feature the Assistant smart speaker feature that lets you control your smart home or office and access the Assistant with a simple &#8220;Hey Google.&#8221; Nest Wi-Fi is one of the best mesh systems on the market and setup is a breeze with the Google Home app. You can also use Nest Wi-Fi with the previous generation of Google Wi-Fi. we use a Nest Router and one point here at the office and the coverage is flawless and fast. data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/GoogleChromebookDevelopmentBoards-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>I remember a day when finding one new Chromebook development board was cause for celebration and excitement.  I remember the thrill of the hunt and the days following a new find, filled with digging and questions around what this new Chromebook would end up becoming.  Those were simpler days and we always knew there would come a time when the number of Chromebooks in development would make it nearly impossible to keep tabs on them all.  <strong>We&#8217;re in that future, now, and the sheer volume of new Chromebooks in development is simply unprecedented.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>We have a post that I&#8217;d recommend you bookmark if you like keeping up with this kind of thing.  As we find new devices in development, <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18348\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">we add them to that single post</a> and try to keep it as updated as possible.  From that single page, you can see all the devices we are keeping an eye on and get a better feel for the absolute mess of Chromebooks that are coming to market in the coming months.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For this post, however, I want to shine a light on a few newer devices we&#8217;ve come across while scouring the Chromium Repositories in search of new features and other Chrome OS goodies.  Like other devices we come across, we know very little about these Chromebooks apart from what baseboard they are built on at this point.  For some of them, details will end up surfacing over time and for others, we won&#8217;t know any other finer points until the device shows up in our office.  It&#8217;s just the way of things and when compared to only having a new board here or there to talk about, I&#8217;d rather be in the midst of this current deluge.  <strong>With that, let&#8217;s look at what&#8217;s new.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<h2>New &#8216;Volteer&#8217; Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The current bell of the ball is &#8216;Volteer&#8217; and the 11th-gen Tiger Lake chips devices built on this baseboard will contain.  These devices will have the option of USB 4.0, Thunderbolt, Intel&#8217;s new Xe GPU, and enhanced performance/battery life.  Just like the current &#8216;Hatch&#8217; Chromebooks we&#8217;ve watched launch in 2020 (Samsung Galaxy Chromebook, Acer Chromebook Spin 713, etc.), &#8216;Volteer&#8217; Chromebooks may show up late in 2020 and will dominate the release cycles in 2021.  Here are the new ones:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2297074\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Lingcod&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2309512\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Lindar&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2327361\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Todor&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2321809\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Eldrid&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h2>New &#8216;Zork&#8217; Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The other big development category right now is the group of devices based on &#8216;Zork&#8217;.  These Chromebooks will be distinctive in the fact that they possess flagship-level AMD APUs that combine powerful AMD chips with Ryzen GPUs.  While we&#8217;ve had a handful of AMD A4 and A6 Chromebooks, the processors inside were budget and meant for affordable devices.  These &#8216;Zork&#8217; boards are meant for bigger, better things and we&#8217;re very excited to see them begin to arrive as the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25260\" target=\"_blank\">movement on Steam gaming for Chromebooks is accelerating.</a>  Here are the newest additions:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2306889\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Dirinboz&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2214445\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Woomax&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h2>New &#8216;Kukui&#8217; Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>&#8216;Kukui&#8217; Chromebooks bring things back to 2020 development and are responsible for devices like the Lenovo Chromebook Duet and 10e.  Those devices only scratch the surface of what we&#8217;re expecting to see in the affordable Chromebook category from this baseboard.  There are many &#8216;Kukui&#8217; boards that have been in the works for quite some time and we&#8217;re adding a few more to the mix:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2319495\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Willow&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2319498\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Burnet&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2319499\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Esche&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h2>New &#8216;Dedede&#8217; Chromebooks</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Finally, our &#8216;Dedede&#8217; family is based on the upcoming Jasper Lake chip set from Intel.  These new chips may not be as flashy as the Tiger Lake chips that are pushing flagship machines, but their smaller process (10nm) and increased speed and graphics will make them awesome chips for mid-range Chromebooks.  The current crop of Gemini Lake Chromebooks are impressive in their battery life and performance at low prices, so we&#8217;d expect even better cost/performance ratios with Jasper Lake when they arrive.  Here are the new additions:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/overlays/chromiumos-overlay/+/2223557\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Drawcia&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2227769\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Boten&#8217;</a></li><li><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2301561\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">&#8216;Madoo&#8217;</a></li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>For now, that is all we&#8217;ve found to add to the <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18348\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">ongoing list of tracked, upcoming Chromebooks.</a>  We&#8217;re always on the hunt for more and we fully expect to see more AMD and Intel Tiger Lake devices pop up for the next few months.  It&#8217;s an exciting time to be a Chromebook fan and we cannot wait to see the fruits of all this labor by the Chrome OS team.  Stay tuned.</p>\n\n\n\n<img src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/patreonInContentDesktop.jpg\" class=\"patreonDesktop\">\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/chromecastAndroidTVdongleSabrina-1024x580.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>We&#8217;ve been talking for months about &#8216;Sabrina&#8217; &#8211; Google&#8217;s upcoming Chromecast/Android TV dongle &#8211; and how this new take on a streaming device from Google will bring together the companies two differing takes on the smart TV market.  With the flexibility of Chromecast from both a use case and hardware standpoint to the more-robust UI and navigation that Android TV offers (there&#8217;s a remote, after all), <strong>this new device could be the best of both worlds when it does show up later this year.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>With <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://9to5google.com/2020/08/23/two-google-devices-fcc-possibly-sabrina-android-tv-remote/\" target=\"_blank\">what appears to be &#8216;Sabrina&#8217; spotted passing through the FCC</a> just last week, it looks like we won&#8217;t be waiting much longer for this new streaming hardware to arrive.  Everyone&#8217;s expectation is some sort of virtual October event from Google to announce their <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-pixel-4a-5g-pixel-5-announcement/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24033\" target=\"_blank\">already-teased Pixel 4a 5G and Pixel 5 phones</a> and it seems a <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/new-google-home-nest-assistant-speaker-fcc-photos/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19879\" target=\"_blank\">new Google Home</a> and this new Chromecast/Android TV dongle will join them.  Who knows, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/halvor-pixelbook-2-chromebook-made-by-google\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25063\" target=\"_blank\">maybe we&#8217;ll see a new Pixelbook, too,</a> but none of that is the point of this post today.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Last night, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://9to5google.com/2020/08/31/google-sabrina-android-tv-price/\" target=\"_blank\">news leaked on the pricing of Google&#8217;s new dongle</a> and what we&#8217;re seeing is super-aggressive for a device that in all likelihood will be more powerful than the existing Chromecast Ultra and will cost less.  It&#8217;s a bit ambiguous at this point, but <strong>three separate listings show a price for &#8216;Sabrina&#8217; between $49.99 and $59.99,</strong> and honestly, anything in that range is pretty amazing for <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-chromecast-ultra-android-tv-dongle-what-we-know/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19275\" target=\"_blank\">all you&#8217;ll get in this single streamer.</a>  Don&#8217;t forget, you&#8217;ll be able to run Android TV apps and do all the standard streaming stuff you&#8217;d do with a regular Chromecast, too.  I see little reason why this dongle won&#8217;t be fully-capable of giving users a great experience for Stadia and NVIDIA GeForce NOW, too.  Slap on Google Assistant support and there&#8217;s not much this little dongle can&#8217;t do.</p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-chromecast-android-tv-remote-sabrina/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-18932\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/chromecastAndroidTVdongleSabrina-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"Why Google&#039;s new Chromecast/Android TV dongle could be a massive hit\" title=\"Why Google&#039;s new Chromecast/Android TV dongle could be a massive hit\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">Why Google&#8217;s new Chromecast/Android TV dongle could be a massive hit</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/robbypayne/\">Robby Payne</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<p>You can see a listing over at <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache:3Jln4-gWfCQJ:https://www.walmart.com/ip/Bundle-Sabrina-Abbey-Rock-Candy-US/403830906+&#38;cd=2&#38;hl=en&#38;ct=clnk&#38;gl=us\" target=\"_blank\">Walmart&#8217;s website right</a> now for the higher price and Android Police&#8217;s <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://twitter.com/ArtemR/status/1300593308201185280\" target=\"_blank\">Artem Russakovskii tweeted about</a> a confirmed Target availability for the same price as well.  The lower-priced leak come from Home Depot where the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://9to5google.com/2020/08/31/google-sabrina-android-tv-price/\" target=\"_blank\">folks at 9to5 Google were able to find a cached version of the landing page for the product and it&#8217;s $49.99 price tag.</a>  Additionally, they had a tipster send them photos of Home Depot&#8217;s internal system showing a full range of colors and pricing, too.  We&#8217;re seeing &#8216;Rock Candy&#8217;, &#8216;Como Blue&#8217; and &#8216;Summer Melon&#8217; in the company&#8217;s inventory, so there will be at least those colors as an option, if not more.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>A streaming device in this price range puts &#8216;Sabrina&#8217; in line with other, similarly-functioning devices from Amazon and Roku, but those devices don&#8217;t have Chromecast built-in and won&#8217;t function as streaming game devices, either.  While many have simply just <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/want-a-chromecast-remote-how-to/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"10044\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">wanted a Chromecast with a remote,</a> &#8216;Sabrina&#8217; looks ready to offer far more than that and, at the risk of sounding like a total fan boy, could easily be the streaming device just about everyone should go out and buy.  <strong>It&#8217;s taken years, but it really feels like Google has figured out its smart TV strategy with this one, and we&#8217;re ready for it.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a 15:33:24","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 15:33:24","title":"Steam gaming on Chromebooks inches closer as new details on install process emerge","link":"https://chromeunboxed.com/?p=25260","description":"<a data-image-title=\"SteamGamesChromebooksWebInstallAppService\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/SteamGamesChromebooksWebInstallAppService-300x169.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/SteamGamesChromebooksWebInstallAppService-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>In 2020, there have been many ways to go about playing Steam-compatible games on Chromebooks.  There have been methods that <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/how-to-install-steam-on-a-chromebook/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18093\" target=\"_blank\">utilize Linux on Chrome OS</a> in a few different variations and then there&#8217;s the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-geforce-now-web-player-exclusive-important\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24901\" target=\"_blank\">NVIDIA GeForce NOW approach</a> that recently became available for Chromebook users, but none of those options are what <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/official-steam-support-could-be-headed-to-chromebooks/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"14334\" target=\"_blank\">Kan Liu was speaking of at CES 2020</a> when he made the statement that Steam support for Chrome OS was officially in the works via the Linux container.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Instead, as we&#8217;ve come to find out this summer, <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/borealis-steam-valve-gaming-chromebook-container-half-life-aperture-science/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19806\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">the path to Steam gaming on Chromebooks will likely take the form of a custom container</a> much like what we&#8217;ll see with <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/parallels-details-emerge-on-how-windows-will-run-on-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"23995\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Parallels and Windows apps on Chromebooks later this year.</a>  It is the same basic method that the Chrome OS team has used to get Linux apps up and running on Chromebooks, but these custom containers can run different operating systems inside and thus, deliver different experiences for users.  For instance, there&#8217;s a ton of work being done on <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-android-11-apps-arcvm-crostini/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">ARCVM, which will be a custom Android container that will bring the Android framework to Chromebooks</a> in a manner far more similar to what we see with Linux apps as opposed to the current ARC++ method we currently have.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>The custom container that the Chrome OS team is building for this Steam experience goes by the name of Borealis</strong> and there are some really fun details that have emerged in the past week from the Chromium Repositories that shed a bit more light on what the Steam experience will be like once it does land on Chrome OS.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>There will be a web-based installer</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>First up, it is becoming clear that there will be a web-based install method for users to get Steam up and running.  This makes sense as the current install method for Steam revolves around <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://store.steampowered.com/about/\" target=\"_blank\">heading to their installer page,</a> choosing your platform, and beginning an install process from there.  From what we&#8217;re seeing in the repositories, <a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2391891\">there will be a web-driven process that will get the entire installer up and running for Chromebooks.</a></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM.png\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25263\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager/screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2-25-19-pm/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM.png\" data-orig-size=\"766,1036\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-title=\"Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM-222x300.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.25.19-PM-757x1024.png\" loading=\"lazy\" Chromium Gerrit</a></figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>As you can see in these strings for the web install flow, there is language about <strong>setup, install, completion, VM configurations, errors, and launching.</strong>  Much of this is similar to the flow we see when Linux apps are turned on for a particular Chromebook and that shouldn&#8217;t come as a surprise.  The bigger deal here is the fact that <strong>this install process looks to be originating from a download via a web interface.</strong>  Ideally, users will click the install button, open a file, and the container install and setup will take care of itself.  It is unclear at this time whether or not the native ability to turn on Borealis will be there in the Chrome OS settings like we see with Android apps and Linux apps.  Since they are clearly setting up a web installer to get things going, I&#8217;d wager the answer is no.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Installed games will be handled like all other apps on a Chromebook</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;d argue that this next tidbit is even more impressive than the web installer.  <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2362102/5/components/services/app_service/public/mojom/types.mojom\" target=\"_blank\">From the looks of what we&#8217;re seeing,</a> Steam games you install via the Borealis method will be standalone apps in your app drawer just like any other thing you install on a Chromebook.  This means that launching the game you just installed will be as easy as opening up Chrome or your Files app and these games will even be able to be pinned on your tray.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25267\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager/screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2-51-05-pm/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM.png\" data-orig-size=\"410,208\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM-300x152.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"410\" height=\"208\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25267\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM.png 410w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Screenshot-2020-09-03-at-2.51.05-PM-300x152.png 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 410px) 100vw, 410px\" /><figcaption><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2362102/5/components/services/app_service/public/mojom/types.mojom\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Even better, your games will be a part of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebook-apps-service-android-linux-install-remove-manage/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"7048\" target=\"_blank\">the App Service</a> that wrangles all the installed apps on your Chromebook, meaning you&#8217;ll have the ability to uninstall via a simple right-click or in the larger Apps menu in your settings.  All told, Steam games will look, behave, and feel just like all the other apps you install on your Chromebook and that will make the entire experience of finding, installing, using and removing them fit into the already-defined way of doing things on Chrome OS.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Borealis has a logo</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>If you&#8217;ve noticed, installed Linux apps that don&#8217;t have a proper logo get the generic penguin as a place holder.  As will be the case from time to time, a game will come along and the icon data either won&#8217;t be there or won&#8217;t be correct.  In those cases, Chrome OS needs a fill-in icon to put in its place.  <a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromium/src/+/2377770\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Thanks to the commit for this,</a> we have a basic, simple idea of what the logo for the Borealis project looks like.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25266\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/steam-games-chrome-os-chromebooks-web-install-app-manager/borealis/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png\" data-orig-size=\"192,192\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"borealis\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"192\" height=\"192\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25266\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis.png 192w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/borealis-150x150.png 150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 192px) 100vw, 192px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Simple, but still pretty cool, right?  This will likely stand in as the icon during the download/install process and will show up in your App menu in settings or in your app drawer any time a game doesn&#8217;t come equipped with a properly-oriented icon of its own.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Still work to be done</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>From the looks of the repositories right now, there&#8217;s likely a ton more work to be done before any of this hits open testing phases.  I don&#8217;t have a timeline in mind, but if we see anything before the end of the year, I&#8217;d be shocked.  Granted, a ton of the VM work and plumbing is already in place thanks to the years of work the Chrome OS team has done on the Crostini Project that brings Linux apps to Chromebooks.  Perhaps as this is simply a modified container, the work won&#8217;t be anywhere close to as intense for Borealis as it was for Crostini, <strong>but don&#8217;t expect anything too soon. </strong> </p>\n\n\n\n<p>It&#8217;s encouraging that tests are happening with the web installer and that we&#8217;re already talking about app icons and inclusion in the App Service, but I&#8217;d say we&#8217;re months out at this point from seeing Steam appear on Chromebooks.  When it does, however, <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-pixelbook-2-halvor-usb-4-thunderbolt\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25252\">Tiger Lake Chromebooks (like the hopeful Pixelbook 2)</a> and maybe even some <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-ryzen-chromebooks-soon-benchmark-score-increase\" target=\"_blank\">AMD-powered Chromebooks</a> will be around and ready to offer up their far-superior GPUs to users, making for some pretty sweet, local gaming action on Chromebooks.  <strong>Who would have ever thought?</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<img rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.patreon.com/chromeunboxed\" target=\"_blank\">we officially launch our Patreon Community!</a></strong>  This has been a move that has been in the works for quite some time as we have looked into all that Patreon has to offer for our readers, listeners, and YouTube viewers alike.  There&#8217;s a little something for everyone and, at the same time, we get the opportunity as content creators to be <em>a bit less ad-funded and a bit more audience oriented.</em>  We tried in the past year to do something similar with YouTube Membership, but the platform simply didn&#8217;t offer all the connections we were after.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-youtube wp-block-embed is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\n<iframe title=\"We&#039;re Officially Launching a Patreon Community: Here&#039;s Why\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/0AbpMgBr91c?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>In the move to Patreon, we now have multiple contribution tiers with all sorts of great options when it comes to ways for us to connect to you all as our audience.  We extended the option of Patreon to our existing YouTube Membership group about a month ago, so we&#8217;ve been able to see Patreon in action already and <strong>it has been an absolute blast.</strong> Probably the group favorite right now is the access to our private Discord server, where the already-growing community is able to not only connect to us here at Chrome Unboxed, but with one another as well.  <strong>It&#8217;s been a ton of fun!</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>There are multiple tiers you can join, giving you access to things like <strong>behind-the-scenes footage, early access to videos, private Discord server access, an ad-free experience on the mobile and desktop versions of the website, your name listed on all our YouTube videos, and monthly live stream Q&#38;A.</strong>  You can head over to <a href=\"https://www.patreon.com/chromeunboxed\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">patreon.com/chromeunboxed</a> to see the breakdown on the different levels to see which is right for you if you are interested.</p>\n\n\n\n<img src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/patreonInContentDesktop.jpg\" class=\"patreonDesktop\">\n<img src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/patreonInContentMobile.jpg\" class=\"patreonMobile\">\n\n\n\n<p>For us, this all means we now have a simple-to-manage, easy-access way to deliver unique content to our most loyal fans and a much better way to interact with each of you.  With comment threads on the site and on YouTube, that just isn&#8217;t realistic and its not a great experience.  With Patreon, we&#8217;re very excited by the potential of this community and where we&#8217;ll be in 6 months or a year from now.  We hope you join and we hope you enjoy it all as much as we&#8217;ve enjoyed preparing all this.  If the last month&#8217;s worth of interactions is anything to go by, the Chrome Unboxed Patreon Community is going to be a fantastic place to be.  <strong>Thanks in advance, and we hope to see you all there!</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet Alerted About New Posts On <br class=\"forMobileOnly\"><span class=\"highlighter\">Your Schedule</span><br>\n\t<a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-pixelbook-2-assistant-key-proof-halvor-tiger-lake\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"24972\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">finding a pretty clear connection to a new Google-made Chromebook in &#8216;Halvor&#8217;,</a> I honestly looked right by another key clue that alludes to the fact that this device very well could be a Google-branded Chromebook.  When it comes down to hardware, there is little to differentiate Google&#8217;s own Chromebooks from those made by other manufacturers apart from hardware keys on the device, and as I was excited by the Assistant key appearing on &#8216;Halvor&#8217;, <strong>I looked right past another important key being included.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>The humble play/pause button on Chromebooks is a relatively-new addition that only began with the Pixelbook.  It is part of what we all thought would be a new keyboard layout for Chromebooks moving forward after the launch of that device.  Oddly-enough, we didn&#8217;t see this particular layout again until the Pixel Slate a year later and not again until the Pixelbook Go a year after that.  There have been a few variations on the Chrome OS keyboard, like what we saw in <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/dell-latitude-chromebook-enterprise-review-expensive-consumers/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Dell&#8217;s 2019 enterprise-focused, VM-ready Latitude Chromebooks,</a> but there have been no other sightings of the exact top-row layout that the Google devices carry on any other Chromebooks.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>While it is worth noting that the two third-party keyboards that have the Assistant key built in (Logitech K580 and Brydge C-Type) also get this unique top-row layout with the play/pause button added, <strong>no Chromebook has come with it built in except Google&#8217;s own devices. </strong> I went back and looked at videos and images of all the Chromebooks we&#8217;ve reviewed in the past few years and, much to my surprise, there was no other device with this setup.  <strong>Until &#8216;Halvor&#8217;, that is.</strong>  <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2366317/5/board/halvor/board.c\" target=\"_blank\">According to this commit,</a> the layout of the keyboard for &#8216;Halvor&#8217; will match Google&#8217;s own Chromebooks down to the last key.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25067\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/halvor-pixelbook-2-chromebook-made-by-google/screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10-06-04-am/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM.png\" data-orig-size=\"464,352\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM-300x228.png\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM.png\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"464\" height=\"352\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM.png\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25067\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM.png 464w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Screenshot-2020-08-31-at-10.06.04-AM-300x228.png 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 464px) 100vw, 464px\" /><figcaption><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2366317/5/board/halvor/board.c#67\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Is this firm proof that &#8216;Halvor&#8217; is made by Google?  No, just like the addition of the Assistant key isn&#8217;t.</strong>  And as I&#8217;m fully aware of the existence of confirmation bias, I can&#8217;t even completely say that I&#8217;m not falling prey to it right now.  I&#8217;m looking in every nook and cranny for more proof that &#8216;Halvor&#8217; is made by Google not because I want to be right (I obviously do), but because I have a deep, deep desire for Google to show up with a Chromebook for us to love this year.  We&#8217;ll keep digging and we&#8217;re hoping we end up finding a smoking gun, but I&#8217;m also prepared to just be a hopeful Google fan going into October this year.  Who knows, may Stephen Hall over at 9to5 Google will just get this device before then and <a href=\"https://9to5google.com/2019/10/10/exclusive-this-is-google-pixelbook-go-gallery/\">leak it all out like he did with the Pixelbook Go.</a>  <strong>A guy can hope, right?</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Shop data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/change-your-password-chromebook.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>I will admit, I do not change my password as frequently as I probably should. That said, there are a number of reasons why one would want to update, change, or reset a Chromebook password. Thankfully, your Chromebook password is tied directly to your Google account and the credentials are one and the same. Perhaps you&#8217;re like millions of users whose email accounts have fallen victim to an unfortunate data breach. Maybe you&#8217;re like me and it&#8217;s just time to update your password for the sake of security. In another, all too familiar scenario, you may have lost or forgotten your account password and you need to reset it to regain access to your Google services. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Today, we&#8217;re going to take a look at the proper methods to change and/or reset your Google password depending on your specific situation. We&#8217;ll start with the easiest scenario and then, move on to the more sticky implementations of changing your password. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you simply want to change your login password for your Chromebook, you just have to update the password associated with the Google account that you use to log in. This is best done from the Chromebook you use regularly. This method takes presumes that you know your current Google password. To begin, open up a New Tab Page on your Chromebook. If you have a custom New Tab Page, you can just go to Google or any of your connected Google services such as Gmail or Google Drive. At the top-right corner, you should see your profile picture. Click the photo and select &#8220;Manage your Google account.&#8221; It will be the one directly below your photo, not the one at the bottom of the dropdown. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure 1024px\" /></a></figure></li></ul></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have multiple accounts logged into your device, double-check to make sure that you are headed to the account you wish to update. You can actually get to this page faster by heading to your personal Google activity URL. Just click this link. <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://myaccount.google.com/\" target=\"_blank\">My Google Account</a>. Pretty cool, huh? Next, you will need to find the password settings. On the left-hand menu, click &#8220;Security&#8221; and the second item in the list should say &#8220;Signing in to Google.&#8221; The top line says &#8220;password&#8221; and that&#8217;s the one you want to click in order to update your password. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-gallery columns-1 is-cropped\"><ul data-carousel-extra='{\"blog_id\":1,\"permalink\":\"https:\\/\\/chromeunboxed.com\\/how-to-reset-the-password-on-your-chromebook-the-right-way\\/\"}' class=\"blocks-gallery-grid\"><li class=\"blocks-gallery-item\"><figure><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-5-1.png\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25151\" data-image-title=\"Untitled-1-5-1\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-5-1-300x171.png\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-6.png\" data-orig-size=\"887,342\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\"
