100vw, 887px\" /></a></figure></li></ul></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You will now be prompted to enter your current password before you can access the security settings. Now you can set your new Google password. <em><strong>Note</strong>: This will require you to sign in with the new password on any device that uses your Google account. That means your phone, PCs that you use with Chrome, and any smart devices that are linked to your Google account may need to be updated with the new password.</em> Once you&#8217;ve saved your new password, there is one last step. Close your tabs and any apps you may have open. Now, power down the Chromebook. This will update the TPM with the new password and you&#8217;re all set. If you&#8217;re like us, you might have more than one Chromebook around the house. Now would be a good time to go ahead and update the password on those devices. To do this, you will need to log into the other devices with the old password. Once you&#8217;ve done that, Chrome OS should prompt you to update your credentials and sign in again. It&#8217;s best to do this sooner than later so you don&#8217;t forget your old password and lock yourself out of a device. That leads us to the next scenario that would have you reset your password. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Lost or forgotten</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>In the event you forget your Google password, I have good news and bad news. In most cases, you can reset the password to your Google account. Unfortunately, your Chrome OS device can only be accessed with the password that you have forgotten. This is why it is imperative that you keep important data and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/backup-and-restore-your-chromebooks-linux-setup/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25047\" target=\"_blank\">files backed up</a> to your Google Drive account, external storage, or some other form of off-device storage. Most Android app data is synced to your Google Play account so that&#8217;s not a real concern but any saved files from the web, documents, applications (Android or Linux) or anything else will be lost forever if it is only saved locally on your device and you have lost your password. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have data saved that you absolutely do not wish to lose, make sure you have a sure-fire way to remember your password. That said, there are some instances where you simply can&#8217;t remember your password. If that is the case, logging back into your Chromebook will require a powerwash. This process will completely erase any data on the device. That includes any other accounts that may be logged into the Chromebook. As you can see, you want to avoid this path unless you have absolutely no other alternative. To get started, you will need access to a PC or even the guest mode on a Chromebook. Navigate to the Google login page and enter the email for the password you need to reset. You can find that page <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://accounts.google.com/signin\" target=\"_blank\">here</a>.  Beneath the password field, click the &#8220;forgot password&#8221; link. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25165\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/how-to-reset-the-password-on-your-chromebook-the-right-way/google-forgot-password/\" data-orig-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"1137,616\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"google-forgot-password\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-300x163.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-1024x555.jpg\" loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1024\" height=\"555\" src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-1024x555.jpg\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25165\" srcset=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-1024x555.jpg 1024w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-300x163.jpg 300w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-768x416.jpg 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password.jpg 1137w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>You will be prompted to try the last password that you can remember for the account. If you want to try an old password, go ahead. You may luck out and the process will continue. If you can&#8217;t think of one, select &#8220;try another way&#8221; and see what options you have. If you have a recovery email, you will be able to send a link to the other email that will let you reset your password. If you have set up 2FA with your Android device, you can choose to verify it with your phone. You will receive a notification on your mobile device asking for confirmation. Hit yes on your phone and your browser should forward you to the page where you can set up your new password. Save that and close your browser. This would be a good time to point out that your Google Account offers a number of ways to back up and recover your account. You should have that setup. Just sayin&#8217;.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, it&#8217;s time to turn to your locked Chromebook. If you&#8217;re logged into your Chromebook, you can powerwash from the settings menu. Sadly, you can&#8217;t log in. If you could, you probably wouldn&#8217;t be reading this. Instead, we&#8217;ll have to do some keyboard gymnastics to reset your device. <strong>Remember, this will delete all data on your device. It will be reset to factory settings.</strong> To reset your device, make sure all users are logged out. from the sign-in screen, press the keys <strong>CTRL+SHIFT+ALT+R</strong>. The powerwash screen will pop up and prompt you to confirm the reset. The device will then restart on go through the reset process. Once it is finished, you will be able to log in with your Google Account and newly updated password. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have a managed device from work or school, these methods do not necessarily work. You will need to contact your IT Admin to see what steps you will need to take in order to reset or recover your password. We will cover those various methods at another time. For now, I hope this helps get you back up and running sooner than later. </p>\n","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 01 Sep 2020 18:48:20 +0000","feedId":7121,"bgimg":"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/change-your-password-chromebook.jpg","linkMd5":"b15a25383b14859a76a604113ecf28a9","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn81@2020_6/2020/09/05/07-33-24-933_c9dd47830af22981.webp","destWidth":1024,"destHeight":614,"sourceBytes":28364,"destBytes":16286,"author":"Gabriel Brangers","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/change-your-password-chromebook.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn81@2020_6/2020/09/05/07-33-24-933_c9dd47830af22981.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-3-1024x563.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn89@2020_5/2020/09/05/07-33-27-141_c5db07d377af8668.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-4-1024x334.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn26@2020_6/2020/09/05/07-33-27-111_ba5098848a2d010a.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-5-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn17@2020_3/2020/09/05/07-33-27-061_973b89828a035e0a.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Untitled-1-6.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn82@2020_1/2020/09/05/07-33-27-429_94107f467bfce407.webp","https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/google-forgot-password-1024x555.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn5@2020_6/2020/09/05/07-33-27-019_bd5d53f39041c1c7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599291204629},{"createdTime":"2020-09-05 15:33:24","updatedTime":"2020-09-05 15:33:24","title":"Surprise! data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/chrome-os-management-print-jobs-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>Yesterday, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/whats-new-with-chrome-os-85-wi-fi-sync-play-pause-video-and-more/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25186\" target=\"_blank\">Chrome OS 85 started rolling out to users right on schedule</a> and with it, there were a number of updates that will make the user experience even more enjoyable. As we had hoped, there are some unannounced features that came along for the ride and one of them blind-sided me this morning. Developers have been <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/printing-scanning-management-app-chromebook/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"15936\" target=\"_blank\">working on print management for Chrome OS</a> off and on over the past few months but I didn&#8217;t think that the feature was anywhere near ready for primetime. <strong>I was wrong. </strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>As one of our <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/patreon-community-launch-chrome-unboxed\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25162\" target=\"_blank\">fellow Chromies pointed out in our Discord chat</a>, Chrome OS 85 added a new app to the launcher called &#8220;Print Jobs.&#8221; Originally branded &#8220;print management app,&#8221; the new feature appears to be a system web app and was recently updated to Print Jobs last month. As you&#8217;d expect, this app will give you a hub for viewing active and historical print jobs. There&#8217;s not a lot going on here at the moment but it does show active and past print jobs. During an active printing session, I was able to cancel the print job which is exactly what you&#8217;d expect this app to do. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25223\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/surprise-chrome-os-85-brings-print-jobs-management-app/screenshot-2020-09-02-at-12-13-02-pm/\" weren&#8217;t expecting to see a print management app in this update but it looks like developers were ready to get this one out the door. This builds on the ongoing updates to Chrome OS&#8217; ability to print with ease. Chromebooks are gaining network access to a wide number of printer types through this evolving process and Print Jobs is a small, albeit important piece to that puzzle. This will be a welcome change for long-time Chromebook users who were once cursed with the inability to install whatever printer they wanted. It will also be a necessary update when Cloud printing finally gets<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/google-cloud-print-shut-down-december-2020/\" target=\"_blank\"> laid to rest in December of 2020</a>. In related news, Chrome OS Canary now lists a &#8220;scanning&#8221; app that should, eventually, allow users to scan directly from their devices without the need to install an app or <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebook-how-to-scan-with-hp-all-in-one-printers/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"2822\" target=\"_blank\">navigate to a web address like you can with HP and other printers.</a>  If you haven&#8217;t discovered the Print Jobs app yet, make sure you&#8217;ve updated to Chrome OS 85 and search the app launcher for &#8220;print jobs.&#8221; I&#8217;m excited to see what other features may be added to this system app in the future. It has definitely been a long time coming. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet Alerted About New Posts On <br class=\"forMobileOnly\"><span class=\"highlighter\">Your data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/AMDchromebooksNewFamilyZork-1024x575.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>It&#8217;s no secret that we&#8217;ve been <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-powered-chromebooks-they-may-be-closer-than-you-think/\" target=\"_blank\">waiting an awfully long time for AMD-powered Chromebooks to show up.</a> Sure, we got a little nibble about a year and a half ago when the low-powered, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/hp-chromebook-14-amd-x360-g1/\" target=\"_blank\">cost-effective A4 and A6 devices showed up,</a> but that&#8217;s not what we&#8217;re really after.  We&#8217;re way more excited by the far-more-powerful Ryzen chips that PCs and laptops running Windows get to take advantage of.  AMD&#8217;s lower prices and similar performance are a great fit for Chrome OS when compared to Intel, but <strong>the path has been long as we&#8217;ve waited for these Chromebooks to arrive.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://browser.geekbench.com/v4/cpu/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&#38;q=zork\" target=\"_blank\">I just came across a new benchmark from yesterday (August 31st 2020) over on Geekbench</a> that tells me we may not be waiting much longer for these devices to finally show up.  You see, back when the original benchmarks showed up for the full-powered AMD Chromebooks, <strong>the multi-core scores didn&#8217;t look so hot.</strong> With most of the current-gen Intel Chromebooks like the Acer Chromebook Spin 713, single-core scores are in the 4000-5000 range and the multi-core scores fall in the 13,000-14,000 range.  When the AMD-powered &#8216;Trembyle&#8217; device showed up in April over on Geekbench, the single-core scores checked out, but the multi-core score was a fraction of what we&#8217;d expect from a true Intel competitor at only 7000-8000. <strong> It didn&#8217;t look good.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Fast forward to this latest benchmark, however, and things are looking far, far better.  With a current score of 4059 on single-core and 13303 on multi-core, &#8216;Trembyle&#8217; (based on the &#8216;Zork&#8217; unibuild) looks way more competitive with the current crop of higher-end Chromebooks.  This is more in line with what we expect of the Ryzen 3700C processor that will ship in many of these AMD Chromebooks whenever they do show up.  Keep in mind, these Chromebooks will also come equipped with Radeon Vega Mobile GPU as well, giving them a graphic leg-up on basically anything else on the market until Tiger Lake Chromebooks start showing up later this year and early in 2021 with Intel&#8217;s new Xe integrated GPUs.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>With these increased scores comes an increased expectation that we&#8217;ll begin seeing Chromebooks with AMD chips inside sooner than later.</strong>  It seems the kinks are getting ironed out for these chipsets and perhaps we&#8217;re finally getting closer to seeing what a Chromebook with an AMD processor and GPU can really do.  It is a general trend to see Chromebook benchmarks get better as they approach an actual public launch, so these score increases likely mean we&#8217;re getting much, much closer to seeing a manufacturer announce an AMD-powered Chromebook.  I certainly hope so.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://chrmshop.com/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"BuyButton\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Shop Best Chromebooks of 2020 So Far on Chrome coming","link":"https://chromeunboxed.com/?p=25207","description":"<a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/snapdragon-7c-chromebook-limozeen-trogdor\" title=\"&#8216;Limozeen&#8217; Chromebook begins src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/snapdragonChromebooksTrogdor-1024x589.jpg\" class=\"webfeedsFeaturedVisual wp-post-image\" alt=\"\" loading=\"lazy\" style=\"display: block; data-image-meta=\"{&#34;aperture&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;credit&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;camera&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;caption&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;created_timestamp&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;copyright&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;focal_length&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;iso&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;shutter_speed&#34;:&#34;0&#34;,&#34;title&#34;:&#34;&#34;,&#34;orientation&#34;:&#34;0&#34;}\" data-image-title=\"snapdragonChromebooksTrogdor\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/snapdragonChromebooksTrogdor-300x173.jpg\" data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/snapdragonChromebooksTrogdor-1024x589.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>It&#8217;s been a minute since we found a new Qualcomm Snapdragon-powered Chromebook beginning development.  For those unaware, <a href=\"http://cheza\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">we&#8217;ve had eyes on a Qualcomm Chromebook for quite a long time at this point.</a>  Originally started with the &#8216;Cheza&#8217; baseboard and based on the Snapdragon 845, the idea of a Chromebook with a Snapdragon processor inside has gone through a few changes over the past couple years as we&#8217;ve all been eagerly awaiting the actual product.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>While we don&#8217;t beleive the Snapdragon 845 chip is in play any longer, much of what the Chrome OS team developed for that chip has been ported over to what we are tracking now in the SC7180 that <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/qualcomm-snapdragon-7c-chromebook/\" target=\"_blank\">we feel quite confidently is the new Snapdragon 7c Compute Platform Qualcomm</a> announced in December of 2019.  <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.qualcomm.com/products/snapdragon-7c-compute-platform\" target=\"_blank\">This chipset</a> makes far more sense for Chromebooks when compared with the phone-focused Snapdragon 845, and since that time, we&#8217;ve uncovered a few more Chromebook development boards that have this new 7c chip inside: &#8216;<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18348\" target=\"_blank\">Trogdor&#8217;, &#8216;Bubs&#8217;, &#8216;Lazor&#8217;, and &#8216;Pompom&#8217;</a> are the current lineup we&#8217;ve had in front of us for the majority of 2020.  There&#8217;s been movement and development happening, but when compared with the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18348\" target=\"_blank\">exploding number of Tiger Lake development devices</a> and AMD-powered boards we are currently tracking, <strong>it began feeling a bit like the Qualcomm Chromebook experiment was stagnating.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<h2>Meet the newest Qualcomm-powered Chromebook: &#8216;Limozeen&#8217;</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Just a few days ago, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2385019\" target=\"_blank\">a new developement board was created under the name of &#8216;Limozeen&#8217;</a> and was a direct copy of &#8216;Lazor&#8217; from the ground up.  This means it will posses the same Snapdragon 7c chip and, from the looks of one of only 3 commits available for this device, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2385020\" target=\"_blank\">it will likely be a convertible and have a backlit keyboard.</a></p>\n\n\n<div class=\"crp_related crp_related_block  \"><h5>more from Chrome Unboxed</h5><ul><li><a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/qualcomm-snapdragon-7c-chromebook/\"    target=\"_blank\"  class=\"post-13421\"><img loading=\"lazy\"  width=\"150\" height=\"150\"  src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/qualcommChromebookBubs-150x150.jpg\" class=\"crp_thumb crp_featured\" alt=\"Why we feel confident a Qualcomm Snapdragon 7c Chromebook is in development\" title=\"Why we feel confident a Qualcomm Snapdragon 7c Chromebook is in development\" /><span class=\"crp_title\">Why we feel confident a Qualcomm Snapdragon 7c Chromebook is in development</span></a><span class=\"crp_author\">  by <a href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/author/robbypayne/\">Robby Payne</a></span> </li></ul><div class=\"crp_clear\"></div></div>\n\n\n<p><strong>The truth is, we don&#8217;t know a ton about most of these Qualcomm-powered Chromebooks at the moment.</strong>  What is more important right now is the fact that new boards are being put into play and that signals the fact that more manufacturers are jumping on board to make Chromebooks with Qualcomm silicon inside.  Assuming it will be on par with something like the Qualcomm 765 we&#8217;re seeing in phones like the OnePlus Nord, the upcoming Google Pixel 4a 5G and Pixel 5, <strong>this chip will outperform all the other ARM-based options for Chromebooks currently available.</strong>  <em>It just needs to get here.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>While the entire Snapdragon-on-Chromebooks effort has been going on long enough to warrant a 2020 release, I still don&#8217;t feel like that is in the cards at this point.  We&#8217;re unsure what is taking so long, but my hope is an announcement of some sort happens sooner than later.  Just like with the aging &#8216;Cheza&#8217; board and its now 2-year-old 845 chip, these Chromebooks need to get released before they become obsolete.  If delays keep pushing these devices back, they&#8217;ll feel out of date by the time they actually arrive, and that&#8217;s never a good look.  Perhaps an announcement at Qualcomm&#8217;s yearly summit in December will bring Chromebooks into the fold in an official capacity and we&#8217;ll see something &#8211; virtually &#8211; from CES 2021.</p>\n\n\n\n<img src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/patreonInContentDesktop.jpg\" class=\"patreonDesktop\">\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet Alerted USI Chairman Peter Mueller over on The Chrome Cast,</a> there&#8217;s a part of the USI (universal stylus initiative) narrative that has been clarified for me that is quite exciting and I&#8217;m so glad to be able to share a bit more detail.  To this point, the only USI pens we&#8217;ve seen are full-sized pens that are meant to live as outer extensions to the Chromebook experience.  While pens like these are great to hold, they aren&#8217;t always the most practical to keep around.  After all, the best pen is the one you have on you at the time, and internally-stowed pens are the ones that find themselves ready for use at a moment&#8217;s notice.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;ve made this argument often and while I&#8217;ve appreciated the growing number of Chromebooks that support the USI standard, the fact that this means you have to figure out a storage solution for that supported pen means that the times I need my pen, I usually don&#8217;t have it close by.  I&#8217;m not an artist or a person who loves handwriting, so my pen is only useful for tasks like signing documents or marking up notes on an image or draft of a document.  The cases for me to get my pen out are not that numerous, so most times I keep the pen in my bag and when the time comes where I might use it, it isn&#8217;t always within reach.  <strong>This is why I love a stowed stylus option.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>And this is precisely why I asked Peter about this &#8216;issue&#8217; during our conversation today.  Worried that USI pens would always be the larger, free-floating pens we&#8217;ve seen thus far, I was dubious that such a pen solution would ever make sense for users like me.  <strong>Thankfully, that isn&#8217;t the case.</strong>  According to Pete, with USI, the protocol is light enough and power-efficient enough that we should begin seeing Chromebooks with internally-stowed pens in the next generation of devices.  While the USI standard does need a bit of power to do all of its magic, a rechargeable pen can get juice when stored inside the Chromebook and always be ready for use when the user needs it.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Apart from our conversation today, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/amd-chromebook-zork-usi-stylus-pen-internal-charge/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"19809\" target=\"_blank\">we&#8217;ve previously found commits pointing to stowed stylus support for some AMD &#8216;Zork&#8217; Chromebooks,</a> but nothing pointing to this feature for Chromebooks in the more affordable range.  That has changed, however, and we&#8217;ve now found proof of internal USI pen storage/charging on at least one &#8216;Dedede&#8217; Chromebook derivative in &#8216;Drawcia&#8217; that we just added to <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebooks-upcoming-development-boards-devices-chrome-os/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"18348\" target=\"_blank\">our master list of upcoming Chromebook devices</a> we are tracking.  The commit is pretty straightforward, but you can see it below along with the commit that shows USI pen support for the same baseboard:</p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>UPSTREAM: mb/google/dedede/var/drawcia: Add elan USI touchscreen</p><cite><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/third_party/coreboot/+/2384903\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>drawcia: enable stylus charging Drawcia has garage stylus, this patch enables stylus charging when stylus present.</p><cite><a href=\"https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/chromiumos/platform/ec/+/2373330\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">via the Chromium Gerrit</a></cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>There are two very cool things happening, here.</strong>  <strong>First,</strong> we&#8217;re seeing more support for stowable, rechargeable USI pens.  Pens that have a recharge method and can be kept safe inside a Chromebook are the right option in my opinion.  Users can always opt to buy an additional, larger USI pen if they want one, but having the built-in stylus always at the ready is obviously a nice touch.  <strong>Second,</strong> we&#8217;re not just seeing this in a flagship device.  &#8216;Dedede&#8217; Chromebooks like &#8216;Drawcia&#8217; will be small-core Intel devices that generally come in at lower prices, so <strong>you can count on internal pens becoming more normalized for even the most affordable Chromebooks once these begin showing up.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>For me, this development and the<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/usi-stylus-pen-chromebook-hands-on\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"25054\" target=\"_blank\"> ease of use we&#8217;ve seen in the first working USI pen we have in the office</a> combine to make me all-in on USI pens for Chromebooks and any other device that begins using them.  Standards are good in many cases, and I&#8217;d argue that a standard pen for electronics is one of those spaces.  I love &#8211; LOVE &#8211; the idea that one day down the road I may be able to pick up my USI pen and begin writing or navigating on any device I have in front of me.  Chromebook, Windows laptop, Android phone/tablet?  Sure.  <strong>One day it will all just work, and I&#8217;m very much looking forward to that.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<img src=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/patreonInContentDesktop.jpg\" class=\"patreonDesktop\">\n\n\n\n<div class=\"newsletterSignupBlock\">\n\tGet Alerted About New Posts On <br On the heels of the company finalizing its merger with Sprint, T-Mobile has been working steadily to expand 5G coverage and get high-speed internet into the hands of as many customers as possible. T-Mobile recently announced a three-part initiative that consists of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.t-mobile.com/business/government/first-responders-connecting-heroes\" target=\"_blank\">free service to America&#8217;s First Responders</a> and the T-Mobile Connect plan that offers unlimited talk and text and 2GB of data for as little as $15/month. <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://prepaid.t-mobile.com/prepaid-plans/connect\" target=\"_blank\">T-Mobile Connect</a> also adds an extra 500MB of data each year for up to five years at no additional cost. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The third and final phase of this initiative comes in the form of a 10 billion dollar commitment to our country&#8217;s education systems. Project 10 Million will span five years and will provide eligible school districts access to free internet for underserved students. This will come in the form of a free mobile hotspot and 100GB of yearly data at no cost to eligible families. </p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p>Education is the great leveler, but without internet access, kids will be left behind. T-Mobile has a big goal – to deliver connectivity to every child who needs it across the U.S. Starting now with our historic Project 10Million commitment, we’re going to help open A LOT of doors to opportunity that might have previously been closed</p><cite><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.t-mobile.com/news/community/tmobile-launches-project-10million-initiative\" target=\"_blank\">T-Mobile</a><a href=\"https://www.t-mobile.com/news/community/tmobile-launches-project-10million-initiative\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\"> CEO Mike Sievert</a></cite></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p>In addition to free internet, T-Mobile is working to make is easier for students to get access to devices. Project 10 Million will soon provide eligible students with tablets, PCs and Chromebooks at-cost to ensure a viable solution for at-home learning. Among these devices are the Samsung Chromebook 4 and the Lenovo 100e Chromebook. Participants in the project can get up to 5 devices at cost per eligible line. </p>\n\n\n\n<h2>At-cost devices</h2>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>Coolpad Tasker tablet</li><li>Samsung Chromebook 4</li><li>Lenovo 100e Chromebook (Coming soon)</li><li>Lenovo 100e Windows PC (Coming soon)</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>To find out if your school has joined Project 10 Million, contact your school administrator. Clock Essential features the same 1.5&#8243; 3W speaker found in the larger clock from Lenovo which means it should be a decent-sounding device. I&#8217;d put my current one up against the Nest Mini any day of the week. Like its larger sibling, the Essential Smart Clock features a USB port on the back for charging your phone or whatever other accessory you have sitting around. I use it to charge my <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/ticwatch-pro-lte-review-the-wearos-smartwatch-for-the-masses-video/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"14708\" target=\"_blank\">Tic Watch Pro</a> and it works perfectly. The smaller display foregoes a touchscreen and instead, offers a true alarm clock style interface. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Like the 4&#8243; Smart Clock, the Essential features soft touch volume buttons on the top of the fabric-encased chassis but this model adds a dedicated alarm button and a play/pause button. Lenovo has also added a &#8220;night light&#8221; to this model to help you navigate your bedroom when you have to get up in the middle of the night. I&#8217;m not sure if this will simply be a sensor-activated brightening of the display or if it actually has an in-built light. You&#8217;ll also get a button on the back for muting the microphone which should be standard on any smart speaker. Like any Assistant speaker, you&#8217;ll be able to control all of your connected things from the Essential and it even has a weather widget on the display so you can keep an eye on the temperature. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Lenovo Smart Clock Essential goes on sale next month and will retail for $49.99. That means we&#8217;ll likely see some really great prices come the holiday shopping season. In the mean time, the larger Smart Clock happens to be on sale at Best Buy right now for the same $49.99. While I definitely see the appeal of this smaller, more discrete model, $50 for the current Smart Clock is a solid deal and still my recommendation. </p>\n\n\n\n<p><a rel=\"nofollow noopener data-large-file=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/12/AcerChromebook715Review-1024x576.jpg\" /></a>\n<p>In general, we shy away from recommending refurbished or renewed devices. That said, there are always exceptions to the rule. If a device makes sense monetarily speaking and you can add a little peace of mind with a warranty, refurbished can sometimes be the best choice. This happens to be one of those deals. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Outside of the Pixel Slate, the Acer Chromebook 715 was one of the first models to hit the market with a built-in fingerprint sensor. The 15.6&#8243; aluminum Chromebook is powered by 8th Gen Intel processors and features an integrated numeric keypad. Woot! is currently offering refurbished Core i3 or Core i5 versions of the Chromebook 715 at a price that&#8217;s significantly lower than a new model. Again, we shy away from renewed devices but in today&#8217;s market, we&#8217;re on the lookout for any and all Chromebooks that are worth buying. It&#8217;s very difficult to find premium devices at all let alone at a decent price. The Acer Chromebook 715 offers a ton of great features and picking up a refurbished model can save you a couple of hundred dollars. </p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-youtube wp-block-embed is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\n<iframe title=\"Hands-On With the New Acer Chromebook 714 &#38; 715\" width=\"500\" height=\"281\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/lYu4BoF7js8?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>If you&#8217;re worried about warranty, Woot! has you covered. You can grab the Core i3 Acer with 8GB of RAM and 64GB of storage for $439.99 and tack on a 1-year protection plan for only $79.99. That nabs you a powerful 15.6&#8243; FullHD Chromebook with a lot of bells and whistles for just under $520 and that&#8217;s a tough deal to beat in the current climate. If you want more horsepower, you can pick up the Core i5 with a whopping 16GB of RAM for $669.99. Woot! usually runs these deals until they&#8217;ve sold out but the last time this model was on offer, it was gone in less than 24 hours. If you must buy a Chromebook and you&#8217;re looking for premium, this is a great option. href=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chromebook-smoother-screen-refresh-ipad-pro-promotion/\" data-type=\"post\" data-id=\"10368\">initial experimental flags for Chromebooks showed up that allowed for higher refresh rates on external monitors.</a>  Prior to this change, Chrome OS was great at extending displays in all sorts of resolutions, but not all sorts of frame rates.  In Chrome OS 85, however, those flags necessary to make these higher refresh rates happen are in the past and the new normal sees users able to connect up their external monitors that support higher refresh rates and fully take advantage of them.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Just today, we hooked up a Chromebook to a monitor in the office and realized that it actually supports more than 60hz and actually has the ability to leverage 75hz.  To be honest, we didn&#8217;t even know this particular monitor had that ability at all, but Chrome OS&#8217; new display settings make finding and changing the refresh rates on your connected monitors a snap.  <strong>Here&#8217;s how to make the changes and see if your monitor is capable of smoother refresh rates.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\"><img data-attachment-id=\"25235\" data-permalink=\"https://chromeunboxed.com/chrome-os-85-refresh-rates-selector-smooth-external-display/chromeos85settingsdisplay/\" 768w, https://chromeunboxed.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/ChromeOS85SettingsDisplay.png 970w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 493px) 100vw, 493px\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Navigate to your settings and head to <strong>Device &#62; Displays &#62; Select your display &#62; Refresh Rate</strong> and you&#8217;ll now have the option to choose all the possible refresh rates that your monitor supports.  Sadly, my daily driver display &#8211; an LG ultrawide 3440&#215;1440 &#8211; doesn&#8217;t support anything higher than 60hz.  After seeing Chrome OS running at 75hz on Gabriel&#8217;s monitor, I have to admit I&#8217;m already considering an upgrade.  There&#8217;s something about that fluid, buttery motion on higher refresh screens that <strong><em>looks so awesome.</em></strong>  If you&#8217;ve never seen it in action, you may want to go and hit up your settings to see if your connected display has the ability to push a better refresh rate.  <strong>Trust me, if it does, your eyes will thank you.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<img
